< text>
Every once in awhile we get to discover & enjoy a memorable food experience.
I had one at Whiskey Flats yesterday. Excellent baby back ribs, but the real stars were the brisket and the collard greens. The brisket was as good, maybe better, than I've had, in the past, in the San Antonio and Texas Hill Country. Smoked over almond wood, to perfection. The collard greens are their unique recipe. Never had collards to match them, ever. There's nothing complicated about this food, but the sheer excellent quality is worth a drive.</text>

A cute little atmosphere and the food was pretty tasty. Cornbread was not dry and the beans and slaw were also good. Ribs I wish were meatier so I would just try something different next time. It‚Äôs nice that they do small business events on certain weekends. I do have to comment on the nutty lady that lives on the corner lol she was cursing and screaming about people not being from Pedro and parking near her drive way. She was sporting a giant bottle of Bombay liquor haha so it could be that. Apparently she tries to cause a ruckus often regardless of the parking. Either way if you haven‚Äôt tried this place out I‚Äôd recommend it. And try to come during a small business weekend then you could also pick up dessert with your meal.< /Text>

<resp>None<//resp><rating>5</rating>< Text>
Best barbecue I have ever had. Their bbq sauce is a perfect balance of sweet, savory acid and heat. The smoked meat is so tender! We took some to a family get together and realized we only had plastic utensils and was worried for a minute but you didn‚Äôt even need a knife.

We got a mix of the brisket, ribs and chicken. I am not normally a fan of ribs. These pork ribs are my exception. Meat just fell of the bone. Loved the rub they use on the brisket! The chicken had a nice smoked char to it.

We had the baked beans and coleslaw as a side. The beans had a nice smokey hint to them and again perfectly balanced the sweetness and savoriness. The coleslaw was perfect to cut through the meal. Not too sweet, and just a little creamy and that hit of acid, just the way I like it.

10/10 definitely recommend!< /Text>

Today, early December 2020, I went to the Oroville DMV office to register and license a used, homemade utility trailer that I bought  in California.  First, I went to the outside intake desk. Then I followed up with the inside window intake staff, then parked my vehicle and trailer at the  parking area for the clerk to "tag" my trailer with an ID sticker.  Next  I went inside to fill out and sign paperwork, pay my registration fees and tax.  I then received my registration paperwork and my new PTI license plate.  The whole process was so smooth and pleasant, and the staff were pleasant and friendly.  No crowds, and no waiting.  I prayed to God prior to going to DMV for a smooth transaction without glitches!  What an answer to prayer.!!!<//Text>

<Review>We were very satisfied patients of Dr. Mobile's for many years, so I recently brought in my 3 yr. old ESA cat for a urinary tract issues. Dr. Singer apparently did an examination without my presence, made a diagnosis (made excuses for not exactly knowing what the problem was,) and without any consultation with me or providing a cost estimate, he administered treatment consisting of LRS fluids subcutaneously (not intravenously. No blood work or urinalysis was performed, but Dasuquin was prescribed for "crystals" in the urinary tract. Dr. Singer was unable to give me any information on the medication and, frankly, told me "they don't really know how or why it works, but it does." I paid approximately $150 and didn't receive an invoice or explanation and breakdown of the charges. He also provided me with Ziploc bag containing a urine specimen jar with a small amount of aquarium gravel, a syringe, and detailed instructions for collecting a specimen which was to be returned to him in 10 days. (The gravel was only a sample, and I was to purchase a large bag of the non--absorbing "litter" to accomplish this. No cost estimates or advices were provided about SUBSEQUENT visitsThe next day, I called to tell them the cat was experiencing significant swelling on the left side of his face. I brought him back in, examined him without my presence again, and gave him an injection of, apparently, antibiotics, citing a temperature of 102.5. An additional $111 was paid, in full.
A week later, my cat is still in distress, presenting bloody urine droplets.  When I arrived, I was asked to pay an additional office exam fee of $54. On a limited income widows benefit, at the end of the month, I explained that I didn't have funds immediately available to cover it and requested to make other arrangements, i.e., waiving all or a portion of the follow-up exam fee, making payment after the 1st of the month, or smaller installments.
Again, the cat was examined in my absence, and returned to me in the waiting room. They told me that because of my "financial hardship," it would be best to take him to the SPCA "because they handle stuff like that." Dr. Singer was sitting at the reception desk when I clarified my request for an accomodation on the billing, not free or low cost services. They explained that without payment of $54 up front, the Dr. couldn't see us. I asked what my prior $250 covered, as this was a follow-up, and for clarification of the diagnosis; had there been a urinalysis, was there a bacterial infection, or an obstruction? I basically wanted to know what I had already paid for and what had been done so I could tell the other vet. With that, Dr. Singer stood up and told the techs to leave so he could handle my questions. He was immediately condescending of my financial position, and suggested that I was irresponsible for the health and welfare of an animal.  I asked him to consider alternative payment plans, and he refused to see us without payment of a $54 exam fee up front.  He then told me to leave and not come back. They provided a printout of the services as Dr. Singer berated me for forgetting that he had "explained" everything to me already. When I asked if we actually knew what the problem was, since the treatments obviously weren't working, and a urinalysis to confirm the appropriate antibiotic for bacterial infection, he refused to answer. He shoved the one-page "report" at me with no further explanation whatsoever. He was arrogant and antagonistic,  and I commented on his level of professionalism. He then made derogatory comments about my character and insulted me, telling me to "get out and don't come back!" I was like, Really? He then followed me out the door to my car, harassing me like I was stupid. I asked him to please back away, go back inside, and stop the rude behavior. He persisted even when I asked him why he was following me outside and wasting his precious billable time.  The bottom line...Dr. Singer failed to provide professional services, and harassed and bullied me when I questioned him.<//Review>< resp>

<text>Warning: some mildly graphic medical details in the post.

I first found West Coast a little over three years ago when I first moved to San Diego.  I knew we were looking to add to our family soon and wanted an office that catered to OB and Gyn needs. I found them pleasant, easy to work with, not pushy with pill based contraceptives like some places I've visited (they give me rare stroke-like migraines so I cannot take them). You do pay for co-pays and such up front so be prepared.

Once pregnant a year later, I was assigned Dr. French whom I met a few times.  Patients do see multiple doctors during the pregnancy, so if you don't like this option, you should go elsewhere.  I was fine with this and appreciated getting to know different doctors.  I had a bit of bleeding early on and they were able to see me right away and confirm that everything was alright, though I had low Iron levels.  I opted for a c-section but was a good candidate for a VBAC having had an emergency one with my first child, but they thoroughly explained all my options and let me really make the decision.

Day of birth I was at Sharp Mary Birch, everyone was really nice and attentive and it went so smoothly in less than 45 minutes!  During recovery on the second day, I had some incision line bleeding and Dr. French recommended a blood transfusion and iron infusion.  Again, she explained the risk/benefit and let me make the choice since it wasn't a medical necessity.  After the procedure, I felt so much better and was glad I made the right choice!!!!

Follow up care at 6 weeks after birth was fast and they really were nice and made sure I was handling the new baby and myself well.  18 months later I am healed well and have a very flat low-line scar. If my insurance through work hadn't changed I would still be with them!

I highly recommend morning appointments and once you start going bi-weekly and weekly to schedule your appointments as far in advance as you can.  It'll make your life easier!  One downside is that their parking lot is kind of the pits, but there is parking across the street at the Sharp-Reese Steely building that is easier to navigate and find a spot.< /text>< Response>

< review>
This review is for the North County office - during my VERY complicated pregnancy, I saw Dr. Meshkat, Dr. Goodwin, Dr. Saffer, and Dr. Chirico. From my second trimester on, I had to be monitored heavily due to my son having a 1:31 chance of Down Syndrome and Intrauterine Growth Restriction. The last two months of my pregnancy, I was monitored several times a week, and each time, the doctors had a plan and always assured me that my son would be okay, even if he had to be delivered early.

He ended up being delivered via C-section by Dr. Hoover, and she did an amazing job. My son was born at 34.5 weeks at just 3 pounds because he was no longer growing in the womb, and his survival is totally attributed to the careful and difficult decisions made by these amazing doctors.

My son had a 3 week stay in the NICU at Sharp Mary Birch and I received several visits from these doctors just to see how we were doing, which meant so much during such a difficult season.

I'm happy to report my son does not have any genetic issues and is a perfectly healthy 4 month old :)

Maria (the nurse) and Beverly (the receptionist) are also wonderful - because of my frequent appointments, they became friends and support for my husband and I!

If we choose to have another baby, it will certainly be under the care of this incredible group of people.<//review>

< Review>

She gave me advice and told me I didn't need a pap since I got one last year and prescribed some lab work to make sure they were within normal limits.  I then received a bill for $250 office visit and over $1000 lab and imaging bills because everything was coded at infertility which is not covered by my insurance.  I called multiple times to see what was going on since I went in for a routine visit and now they code everything so it's not picked up by my insurance.  Even sharp lab told me to postpone paying and call my insurance since routine lab work would be covered. BEWARE of West Coast OBGYN and Dr. Goodwin!!!  My wife and I are first time expectant parents and picked West Coast Obgyn and Dr. Goodwin because we thought that since they were next door to Sharp Medical Center (top rated in SoCal) they would be a good office. My wife had had a miscarriage months back so we were very anxious to find out if our current pregnancy was healthy.  After sending us off to multiple expensive blood tests and ultrasounds (we are paying out of pocket, mind you), all we get is to speak with are the doctor's assistant nurses (not even nurse practitioners)--and I should mention that we had to hound their offices with calls three times a day before someone would call us back with results!!!

My wife and I almost NEVER write reviews, but if this one will spare other people the pain we went through with West Coast OBGYN and Dr. Goodwin, then it was well worth the time. Went to Oku for my girlfriend‚Äôs birthday (5/3/21). Just the two of us on a Monday night. It wasn‚Äôt terribly busy, but they said they had to seat us inside because the three open tables outside were reserved. Waiter Nick was a little slow to greet us, but we didn‚Äôt wait too long. Ordered a bottle of wine and the Korean cauliflower (which is a little spicy and excellent).
Went on to order two rolls and two plates of sashimi all at Nick‚Äôs suggestion (thanks Nick!).  But here is where the issues begin.
Apparently, we were given the wrong menu, we had an outdated one from days earlier, so the prices were wrong. However, the prices were only off by a few dollars. No big deal right?
The bigger issue is that the menu itself is very confusing and feels a little like a trick.
According to the waiter and manager (after we received our bill and questioned it) there are two parts to one section of the menu, one for nigiri and one for sashimi and the prices for the fish are meant to reflect the difference. However, the menu is set up this way:
14 Toro  -  Tuna Belly 38
12 Hon Maguro  -  Blue Fin Tuna 30
Etc.  (see picture of the menu)
To our surprise the numbers next to the fish are not actually their prices. The numbers on the left are for the nigiri and the price on the right is for the sashimi for BOTH FISH on the line.
That fact was not explained to us and caused quite a bit of confusion when it came to figuring out the bill.
None of this would have been that bad if they had apologized and done the right thing of giving us the expected prices. We wouldn‚Äôt have ordered the second sashimi in the first place if we had known the pricing set up as we were already full. If they had done the right thing, we would happily return to the restaurant, but they didn‚Äôt and we won‚Äôt.
Finally, when ordering the rolls we asked if we could get the Tuna roll regular instead of spicy, and it turns out that it costs two dollars extra, but this isn‚Äôt on the menu.
In the end, a nice night ends with a blip of frustration all over multiple screw ups with a menu. Oh well.< /text>

<username>Sean Gillin</username><gmapID>0x80e9138c25baaaab:0x105ceb813a43cbe<//gmapID><userid>105184419265886504199< /userid><Review>Great sushi, service and a view.</Review><rating>5< /rating><Date>1591500235164< /Date></record>

<userid>102734030539300367732< /userid>< user_name>
Richard Heilman</user_name>
<Time>1570733303166</Time><rate>5<//rate>< Review>
Wonderful ambiance and you have your choice of comfortable inside dining, including two different bars, or a lower patio and a rooftop patio with great views of the waterfront. Dogs are welcome on the lower patio. The fusion menu is varied and interesting, utilizing top-notch ingredients and artful presentations. The wine list is small, but includes a number of good choices. One side of the menu is traditional and modern-interpretation sushi and rolls, while another side of the menu features a number of interesting dishes which are Asian in concept. We ordered the A5 Wagyu that came with five different dipping sauces and grated REAL Japanese wasabi, plump pork gyoza, Saigon chicken wings, halibut & crab "lollipops", shrimp bao "sliders" (more like tacos) , and sticky beef salad. With the exception of the bao sliders whose shrimp filling was pretty "fishy tasting", and the sticky beef, which was rather dry and bland, the food was excellent. Friendly and efficient service throughout the meal. A fine new addition to the Santa Barbara dining scene and certainly one of the best restaurants in town.< /Review>
